SILSOE v. MAULDEN.—The return match was played in West Park, Silsoe, on Thursday afternoon, Silsoe again proving victorious by nearly 100 runs on the first innings. For the winners, J. Gray made 30, M. Squire 23, H. Squire 18, and A. Bottoms 16 not out. Maulden were dismissed for 19, Oudin taking 6 wickets for 6 runs, and P—ter 3 for 10 runs. In their second innings, Maulden compiled 37 for 8 wickets.

HOUGHTON C.C.: MARRIED V. SINGLE.—Played at Houghton on Monday. Score:—Single, 39; Married, 100 for seven wickets.

MESSRS FORDAR'S EMPLOYEES.—A match between the employees of Sewell Lime Works and Blow's Down Lime Works was played at Houghton Green on Saturday, and resulted in a win for the Sewell men by one run, the scores being 61 and 60 respectively.

ST. MATTHEW'S v. ST. MATTHEW'S (LUTON).—Played at Luton on Saturday. Score:—St. Matthew's, 61; Waterlow's, 114.

DUNSTABLE 2ND XI. v. MARKYATE STREET.—Played at Cheverells on Saturday. Rain considerably interfered with the play, and when Dunstable had made 70 for the loss of two wickets, the villagers declared they had had enough of it, and stumps were drawn.

G. Tompkins and A Sturman did not bat.
DUNSTABLE SECOND ELEVEN v. MARKYATE STREET.—This return match was played on the Cheverells Park cricket ground, by kind permission of Mr. B. Bennett, on Saturday. Dunstable had choice of innings and batted first, Anderson and Elliott going to the wickets. Four runs only had been scored when play was interrupted by heavy shower. After a while the game was re-commenced, and good stand was made by the batsmen, the wickets being kept intact until 66 were scored, when Elliott was dismissed, and Anderson followed three runs later. Giddings and Beasley were settling down for run getting, when play was again interrupted for five minutes by a shower, at the end of which the villagers refused to again take the field, urging as an excuse that there was no likelihood of dismissing the Dunstable team that day. Not even the promise to declare with 10 more runs added was sufficient to induce them to take the field, and the game was therefore left in the following position:—Dunstable—W F Elliott, c and b Lee 27; O G Anderson, b Lee 34; T Giddings, not out 8; J Beasley, not out 8; extras 7; (2 wkts) 76.

DUNSTABLE BOROUGH GAZETTE: WEDNESDAY 14 AUGUST 1895-4.

OUR CAPTAIN.

MR L. O. R. THRING.

If there is one man to whom, more than others, Bedfordshire cricket owes its revival, and to might almost say its modern birth, that man is the genial and popular head-master of the Dunstable Grammar School, Mr L. C. R. Thring. When, in 1888, the subject of our cricket took up the residence in our midst, the term “ cricket ” was practically a misnomer for the game which was played in what has often been called the “ sleepy county.” Save for the amateurish expeditions with which we were favoured once or twice every year, and the last little better exhibitions given by our townsmen, “ ye manly olde game ” had died a natural death. There was then no county cricket club, we could boast for county cricket neither of the willow, and as a county we were far in the rear as regarded “ England’s national game. But better times were coming. Such a delightful state of affairs was intolerable to the indefatigable and energetic spirit whom life’s best time became interwoven with ours, and not many months elapsed ere we hailed Bedfordshire folk, as then a renaissance was dawning. Space will not permit us to follow minutely our worthy leader in his herculean task of reviving the all but dead passion, under it he set him, mainly through his persistent efforts and untiring zeal, the game became once more established, the County Cricket Club was formed, and a county team of which from the first we have had cause to be proud, was put into the field.

Hearing these historical facts is mind, we came to the conclusion that a short biographical sketch of “ our captain ” would be of the greatest interest to our readers, and, fully intent on “ button-holing ” the ardent cricketer, we wended our way the other evening to the scene where he and such like spirits do congregate together. It was after a hard day’s work behind the wickets, and when these pleasant white-coated gentlemen had, to the relief of all parties concerned, reluctantly pocketed the balls, that we gained our victim, stalking in his manly, characteristic strides across the sodden turf. A really aroused furore, and various winding ancillary movements at last brought us into close quarters, and then, boldly running him to earth, with a decidedly menacing and aggressive air, we whipped out our note-book and pencil.

What a perfect horror some of our public favourites have of the interviewing fiend! And is that heights will they not to its vain endeavours foisted him! Thus it was with the subject of our sketch. Poor fellow! Had he but known that the uncanny scene which Freeman may call to their aid in order to utilise their ends, he would at once have assured that docile, Harry-like approach, and submitted like a gentle lamb to the trying ordeal.

“ Ah, yes! I know what you want,” with a ghastly attempt at a smile. “ I first saw the light at Uppingham in 1863, and from there——”

“ Half-a-minute, please. You were living at Uppingham?”

“ With my father, the Rev J. C. Thring, who was then Head Master of the Uppingham Grammar School. We remained there until I was two years of age, when we left for Bedford in Wiltshire.”

“ And your early education?”

“ My earliest education was derived from my father. At nine years of age I returned to the Uppingham School, where too not under years of my life were spent. I left there at the time of the fever, and at 13 I was sent to Marlborough.”

“ It was here, I believe, you first learned cricket?”

“ Quite so. Of course I had previously handled balls out and in, but it was at Marlborough that I was grounded in the game. I met with Ashley good success, and at 17 I was in the eleven.”

“ When did you play your first county cricket?”

“ In 1880. I was playing in the Wiltshire team, and we were pitted against South Wilts. I believe in my first innings I knocked up 20, but in my second venture only four came to my credit.”

“ But that was pretty good for a colt. From Marlborough you went to Cambridge?”

“ Yes, but year I went to Cambridge, but I did very little of cricket there.”

“ We know the reason. It was our victim’s innate modesty which led him to seek to hide the truth from us. Did those who know anything about L. O. R.’s brilliant career at Cambridge will easily guess that he had very little time to waste over leather-baiting. Not we let him have his way, and assuming an innocent look, continued:

“ And where after Cambridge?”

“ After leaving Cambridge I took a mastership at Wellingborough Grammar School. There I played a good deal of cricket. The master’s eleven was an exceptionally strong team. I was a master to Wellingborough in 1884, and I made three runs at Wellingborough than in any other period of my cricketing career.”

“ What was your top score there?”

“ Well, as far as I can remember, it was when we were playing the Old Boys team. That day I scored 221.”

“ Ah, you and that is when you ‘ hit the top ’ as uncle Jonathan says. But now I think we will come to nearer home.”

“ As you please. I came here in 1888. Soon afterwards the County Club was formed, and I have been hon. sec. and captain of the team from its start.”

This was really disappointing. We had hoped to hear the “ orthodox ” account of how he brought about that happy state of affairs, and here he was “ closing it over ” without a word about himself. But our victim was already showing signs of suspicion, and fearing lest we should prematurely lose our prey, we varied the plot.

“ Is it not a fact that you have been at the top of our county batting averages every year since the club’s inauguration?”

“ That is quite so. My best performance in county cricket was last year, when we were playing ourselves with the M.C.C. I went in first on that occasion, and played through the whole of the innings, my record at the end being 137 not out.”

“ I believe you made 84? W. W. Bunde gives a brilliant display of batting?”

“ Yes. I was playing for Wiltshire against the M.C.C. when Maude made a century in each innings against us. In that match I met with a goodly amount as a bowler. Right directs fell to my share for 40-runs, and this out of a total of 300 up against us.”

“ Which do you consider your best county season?”

“ Well, taken as a whole, I think last year was about the best I have had yet. At one time last season I had made 560 runs for 000 out. I have not had such good luck this year.”

But the subject of our sketch was fast becoming unmanageable. Making a desperate fight to the end we rapidly fired on our remaining questions :

“ Might I ask you say? Well I am St. Clare, I walk about 11 stone, and really my motto I am not too inquisitive.”

We took the gentle hint, and cordially thanking our genial captain for his courtesy, we departed.
A. W. M.

A match was played at Chara Camp on Wednesday

the score being :—Hooklip, 99 ; Woburn, 76.

DUNSTABLE BOROUGH GAZETTE: WEDNESDAY 21 AUGUST 1895-3

DUNSTABLE TOWN FIRST ELEVEN v.
ASTON CLINTON.
Played at Aston Clinton on Tuesday, and resulted in
an easy win for the visitors by 146 runs. For the
winners Manton and Anderson made a splendid stand
for the first wicket, putting on no fewer than 104 runs
before being parted, when the former left for a steadily
played 67. No other principal scores being Giddings 36,
Staunton 32, Andrews 28, Pepper 24, and 30 standing
to the credit of “Mr Extras.” The home wickets fell
very quickly before the bowling of W. F. Brown.
Langley for the home team batted well for 25, and a
stand of nearly an hour’s duration was made by Chesnall
and Pitt, but only 30 runs were added to the score, the
play during this time being very slow and monotonous.

TOWN SECOND ELEVEN v. CARTER'S C.C.
The low second eleven added one more to their
long list of victories, on Saturday last, on the
town ground, by defeating Carter's C.C. by 45
runs after a good game. The home batting was
fairly good, the principal scores being Love 31,
Gray 21, Tompkins 14, Poulton 10, and Wright 18
(not out). On the visitors' side Hunter played
well for 21, as also did Mooring and Tims for 11
and 10 respectively. In bowling Giddings for
Carter's took six of the town wickets at a small
cost, while the wickets of the visitors were equally
divided among four of the home bowlers. Score,
a follows:-

DUNSTABLE VOLUNTEERS v. LUTON
DETACHMENT.
This match was played at Luton on Saturday,
and resulted in an easy win for Dunstable. Luton
batted first, and were all disposed of for 19 runs,
owing to the very successful bowling of Corporal
Hall. Dunstable scored 71, the bowling by El
Roby. The best scores for the winners were made
by Corporal Smith and Private Booker (21 each).
The following comprised the Dunstable team:-
Colour Sergt. Stills, Sergt. F. Ramsbottom, Sergt.
W. D. Hamilton, Corporal Smith, Private Booker,
Private Sharratt, Private Bonham, Private Burch,
Private Darby.

DUNSTABLE SECOND ELEVEN v. CARTER'S C.C.—
The long list of victories won by the Town second
eleven was augmented on Saturday by another win,
when Carter's C.C. was defeated on the Town ground,
Aslor's-road, by 40 runs. The batting of the
homesters was good, Messrs. Love, Gray, Tompkins,
Poulton and Wright played a good game. For the
visitors H. Bunker played well, as also did E. Mooring
and J. Timm. Scores:—

READING OBSERVER: SATURDAY 25 MAY 1895-4
CRICKET.
IMPORTANT TO SECRETARIES.-As in former years. we readily grant a portion of our space for cricket match reports, but we must impress upon secretaries the importance of sending in the score as soon as possible; after matches are played. We further desire to intimate that no scores can be inserted unless it is written legibly, and the innings set out in the form in which the matches are published. Sheets for drawing up reports can be obtained gratis on applying at the Observer Office. Notices of forthcoming matches will be inserted at the top of our cricket column at the rate of 1s. for each insertion. Match cards, posters and bills of all kinds are printed with the utmost despatch and on strictly reasonable terms at the Observer Office.

† Innings declared closed.
The eleven has played 23 matches, won 12, lost 6, and drawn 5, having scored 3,303 for 207 wickets, an average of 16 25 runs per wicket, against 2,371 for 232 wickets, an average of 10 22 per wicket, by their opponents. Four times they scored over 200, six times over 150, and six times over 100, whilst their rivals never reached 200 and five times exceeded 150, and six times exceeded 100. The highest score was 253 for 7 wickets, and the lowest 60. The highest score against them was 178 for 7 wickets, the lowest 55. R H Jackson has taken 14 catches at the wicket, while in the field H A Turner caught 10, A T Clift and F W Paffit 8, and F G Clarke and J Hodge 7.

The following also played:—L E Todd, 20 runs for 3 innings; W Hatt, 22 for 1; R H Morsley, 3 not out; H V Plumell, for 2; J A Wickham, 6 for 3; H S Davis, 6 for 2; R A Colvin, 11 for 2; B R Dodcock, 17 for 4; A H Bateman, 0 for 2; F Poulton, 33 for 3; H Ravenscroft, 4 for 1; W Fox, 5 not out ; E Rivett, 4 for 1 ; H J Lowsley, 1 for 3 ; W G Mousley, 0 for 1.

[* Signifies not out.]
Regarding the abilities of the players the following should prove of interest:—R. H. Jackson(1892-5) captain. Very useful behind the wicket, and is a sound enough if not a steady correct, and reliable, but not powerful.—J. Hodge(1892-5). A much-improved bowler, a brilliant field. A really good bat with a variety of strokes, but was for one excellent innings has lamentably failed.—A. T. Clift(1893-5). Is an untiring bowler and has done some good performances. Very sound field. Bats with great nerve and hits hard and clean.—R. H. Morris(1893-5). Has improved somewhat in the last few matches, but earlier he showed nothing of his old form.—F. G. Clarke(1892-5). Very steady and useful bat. Fine fielded, but apparently all through the season—H. A. Turner(1895). Has not realised his promise of last year; has, however, improved, and it does his credit.—P. L. Moxley(1894-5). Has abundantly justified expectations. Has a note style and has played some excellent innings. A very clever cover-point.—W. Hatt(1895). A painstaking lad with a nice off drive and a thoroughly reliable point. If possessed of great promise.—W. Hatt (1895). A good left-handed bowler. Has improved in the field.—L. E. Todd (1895). A plucky bat, but lacks judgment. A good clean field when the ball comes straight to him, but does not start soon enough.—R. H. Mousley (1895). An erratic change bowler, very fair field and muscular bat.

READING STANDARD: FRIDAY, 2 AUGUST 1895.-2.

Biscuit Factory B XI v White Cross (Basingstoke).- 
On the Factory club ground on Saturday. The home team
batted first and ran up the respectable total of 131 runs,
mainly owing to the batting of Crook, Povey and Leaver, the
former especially punishing the bowling, C Moorlock on the
than seven 4's in succession. In the bowling department,
honours fell to W H Phillips, who took eight wickets for
eight runs in nine overs. The visitors on following on, made
much better stand, scoring 51 for the loss of two wickets.

Aldermaston v. Mortimer.-A closely contested game was
played in Aldermaston Park on Saturday between the Alder-
maston and Mortimer Clubs; the home team won by three
runs. Owing to the heavy rains the wicket favoured the
bowlers, and in consequence the totals were small. For
Aldermaston Mr O E Keyser and E H Ackerman obtained the
highest scores with 22 each. For Mortimer, Dobree, Wilson,
and Guilding secured double figures. Ten, but not other,
returns were, by the kindness of Mr and Mrs Keyser,
provided for the players and visitors who witnessed the game.

Heath End v. St Lawrence's (Reading).-At Heath End
on Saturday, the result of a highly enjoyable game being an
easy win for Heath End by 85 runs and two wickets. The
batting of Maxwell, White and W Hunt was exceedingly com-
mendable, Maxwell innings of 72 runs being mostly with
two mistakes only. The bowling of Maxwell and Roberts was
superb, Roberts analysis reading seven overs, three maidens,
nine runs and five wicket; and Maxwell, thirteen overs,
maidens, fourteen runs and three wickets. After the match,
through the hospitality of Mr Hunt, the players partook of
tea on the lawn. At the conclusion of the meal the captain
of the home club (Mr E J Hunt), presented Mr H Roberts
with a cap in recognition of his recent performance of the hat
trick. Mr Hunt referred in eulogistic terms to the excellent
services rendered by Mr Roberts, who, in reply, thanked the
club for their kindness. Score :-

Guildhall v Newtown.-On the Newbury ground on Sat-

dozen runs. Allsop was the best batsman, playing well for

Berkshire Chronicle: Saturday 10 August 1895-2.

READING CRICKET WEEK.

A new departure in connection with the Reading Cricket Club has been inaugurated this year in the direction of a cricket week. The matches have been played during the last few days, and this cricket week has been a conspicuous success. Reading have been able to rely on excellent teams for each of their matches, and powerful exponents of the summer pastime met Capt. Nepean, Mr L. G. A. Collins, Mr H. J. Collins, Mr W. O. Nares, Mr F. E. Chapman, Rev C. E. Chapman, F. W. Fynole, F. Down Pundrett, makepeace, &c., and some interesting cricket has been witnessed.

First Match-v. Marylebone C.C.

The week opened with the annual fixture against the M.C.C. The visitors had the assistance of four professional, Blandford, Peck, Sherwin, and Ryette, and two members of the Reading Club, Mr P. T. Baker and Mr Wm. Greenfield. Mr C. T. Murdoch, M.P., captained the visiting team.
Inclement weather greatly interfered with the game, and it had to be finally abandoned. Reading went in first to bat, and thanks mainly to A. Finch (35), H. J. Collins (25), L. G. A. Collins (27), succeeded in compiling 186 runs for nine wickets, when they declared their innings closed. M.C.C. then went in, but after scoring 15 for one wicket, stump were drawn owing to the rain. Mrs Murdoch kindly entertained the teams at lunch and tea. In addition to Mr Murdoch, M.P., Mrs Murdoch and party, there were present Mrs Arbuthnot, and Mr and Mrs Polk, Mr Stanley Peto and party, the Misses Finch, Mrs James Simonds, Miss Maurice, Mrs W. O. Nares, Mr Sidney Laurie, Mrs Hayward, Col. Taylor, &c. The following were the scores:-

Second Match-v. Mr C. E. Keyser's XI.
Mr C. E. Keyser, of Aldershot, who is an ardent cricketer, brought through reading to Reading on Tuesday to play the local eleven. Mr Keyser's XI included G. McCorquodale, Newberry, A. Finch, S. H. Sharrard, and W. M. Greenfield, of Reading. Reading were unsuccessful in winning the toss, and their innings was marred for the fine display of batting by Mr L. G. A. Collins and Capt. Nepean, who made 141 and 105 respectively. When the score reached 301 Reading declared their innings closed. Mr Keyser's XI. began well, but the rain set in and stopped the play, and the innings closed for 105. Reading winning easily by 196 runs and four wickets. F. W. Fynole took three wickets for 25 runs, Pott three for twenty, and Collins two for 4. The Reading Cricket Club provided lunch and tea for the teams. Amongst those present at the match were Mr J. Macfarlane (forward, Rover v. Gillman (Shamrock), Colonel Taylor, Mr E. Sturge, Miss Curwood, Mr Claude Curwood, Mr J. H. Siddall, the Misses Finch, Mrs James Simonds, and Miss Simonds. Scores:-

READING STANDARD: FRIDAY 23 AUGUST 1895-2.

READING v. ABINGDON.—That the cricket field is one of the favourite haunts of King Chance was evidenced beyond doubt in this engagement, which was decided at Reading on Saturday. On the occasion of the first match, played a year ago, the visitors, Reading were represented by a fairly powerful combination, nevertheless they were easily beaten by a decisive margin. But on Saturday to all appearance a mild surprise in the engagement was despite that their eleven on paper was particularly weak they returned the compliment they received at Abingdon with slight interest, Inasmuch as they secured more than an innings’ victory. The home captain ordered his colleagues to the wicket at 10.40, before breakfast, Campion ceased their partnership 11 runs had been obtained. No serious adventure was ridged was recorded before the promising G. Williams handled the willow, he going to third wicket down. Between the third and fourth diminished 82 chalks were added, but after that stage no rapid scoring was chronicled, and with the exception of the veteran Hayward’s easy at a trifle, 143 was the total. Williams with a score of 41 was the not out, the other chief contributors were T. Crowhurst (17), Campbell (32), Pott (10) and E. Eynott (11), each of whom provided a good exhibition. On the visitors taking to attack of Campion and Eynott, it was not difficult to foretell the life of their was stated after but a few minutes play. Dandridge, who is generally looked upon a safe bat, was caught when on run only, and then three wickets were down before ten runs had been made. Lovett scored four, but in doing so had many fresh partners, as might be gathered from the remark that at the fall of fourth wicket the total was 13; five, 14; six, 18; seven, 20; eight, 20; nine, 35; ten, 80. On following on, the visitors started in healthy style as the first wicket realised 29. After this, however, the remainder in the first innings was again apparent, as the board showed that in their second innings only 63 were compiled, of this number Dandridge notched 22 and A. B. Morland 13. So splendidly did both Campion and H. Eynott trundle, that the home captain was content to rely on the twin only in the trundling department that his judgement was sound was demonstrated by the capital record each secured, who in an innings produced: Campion in the first innings bowled 48 balls, and secured one maiden and six wickets at a cost of twenty runs, and in the second delivered 63 balls, and again secured six wickets for 34 runs. Eynott’s analysis read: First innings, nine overs, three maidens, 13 runs and four wickets. Second, twelve overs, three maidens, 25 runs, four wickets. Score:-

READING STANDARD: FRIDAY 23 AUGUST 1895-3.

Guilford C.C. v Newtown C.C.—These clubs met on Saturday in their return fixture at Sandeford park. The game, which ended in a win for Guildhall, was remarkable for low scoring, the bowling taking everything before them. In addition to which the fielding of both sides was good. Humphries and Lucas for Guildhall bowled splendidly, the former capturing 12 wickets for as many runs, and the latter 7 for 13. At the conclusion too, the bowling honours for Newtown. The teams were entertained on the ground, and hearty vote of thanks was accorded to J C Cuthbert and Lady Butler (who were present) for their kindness, also to Mr Alsop. Score:—

Parish Church Institute v Highclere.—The return match between these teams was played by kind permission, on the cricket ground on Saturday in splendid weather. Highclere winning the toss decided to bat first, but owing to the bowling of Gunning and Gayfer, the first four wickets fell for 21, when Collins came in and made a useful stand, necessitating several changes in the bowling. Still runs came, Collins doing the lion’s share, but Gunning going on at the top end fairly beat him with a beauty, whilst the Thirkill made some useful stands. After the interval the Institute started batting with Cook and Pyke, the former hitting his wicket, whilst Pyke contented himself by keeping up his wicket. Maginn the next man, made things more lively putting on 18 in quick time. The other home team double figures were Pyke, Young and Gunning. Both teams were entertained to tea, through the kindness of Mr Godding and Mr H Godding. Score:—

Speen v Burghclere.—This match was played at Speen on Saturday. Newbury v. 49th Regimental District.—The return match between these two elevens was played on Wednesday on the grounds of the former. In perfect cricket weather. The Regimental side got together a score, after one first to bat, and Brooman and Suter Crooke facing the delivery of D. Willis and H. Dull. The former increased steadily, and an excellent catch by Suter at a crucial time for the men when he had reached 24, and Brooman’s wicket went down, 22 was registered. But the rest of the line-up quickly disappeared, and the whole side was all out before lunch for 72. The bowling too short and too often, was not at its best, his best hit being a couple of three and ten fours, all only once. On going to the wickets, they had merely 33, and Croome’s? fine bowling gave opened their innings shortly after their tea interval. J. Hill and Day opposing the bowling of Fielding and Crooke, when run and quickly. It was not until the score had reached 75 that Middlton recovered the position. Willis and H. Dull completely mastered the bowling, the latter being the top scorer. Two for 76. Ingram joined to bat before 42% o’clock. Wells all out. Their results? the fielding was faultless; several changes of bowling were tried by ——, and, to bring about the desired effect, stumps had to be drawn at 6.16 owing to the Reading men having won the toss by 34 runs, the score standing at 103 for no wicket. The 49th no-go? Wells (62) and Ingram (45) never in danger of batting. They were at the wicket last over an hour, during which time they put on 115 runs. ABINGDON HERALD: SATURDAY 7 SEPTEMBER 1895
ABINGDON CRICKET AND FOOTBALL
CLUB.
CRICKET SEASON, 1895.
Matches arranged, 21; played, 17; won, 8; lost, 7;
drawn, 2; scratched, 4. The average of the 1st XI.
in both batting and bowling is appended.
It will be noticed that the club captain, Mr. P. D.
Curtis, heads the batting list with an average of
24.50, Payne and Wilton coming next with 16.33
and 16.25 respectively, while Dandridge, Allin, W.
Legge, F. H. Pryce and Skinner all get into double
figures. Messrs. A. C. M. Croome and F. Deane
improved once each, and scored over the century, 117
being Mr. Croome's score and 109 Mr. Deane's. In
the bowling Payne, Dandridge and E. G. Chaudler
have borne the brunt, the former taking 27 wickets at
an average cost of 5.37 runs, Dandridge 49 at an
average of 7.97 runs, and Chandler 37 wickets at an
average of 9.02; all very good performances. Messrs.
W. T. Morland, Wilson, Lovett, Legge and Ward have
all repeated useful service in this department.
Though the 1st XI. have achieved successes over
Oxford City and Reading, they have not done so well
generally, as in other years. The worst feature of
this year's proceedings is the number of matches
scratched. This we consider a bad omen for the club,
as the reason given for the scratchings is the inability
of the officials to raise teams. This ought not to be
with any club having so many playing members on the
books. Each member is supplied with a fixture-list at
the beginning of the season, and as the success of the
club should be the first thought of all members we
greatly wonder at so many members engaging to play
other matches on dates fixed for club matches, but
to this can be traced the falling off in the 1st XI. per-
formances. If all the subscribing members would pull
together, the Abingdon Cricket and Football Club
would never lack a team, either 1st or 2nd, that would
fail to uphold the honour of the club and the town
which supports it, and we hope in future there will
be no difficulty in this particular direction. We
heartily congratulate the club on the success it has
so far achieved and the members may be assured that
if the remedies prescribed are properly applied there
is a brilliant future in store.

THE SECOND ELEVEN
although not so successful this year as last, have been
able to win more matches than they have lost, and in
three cases out of five, had time permitted the drawn
games to be played out the gains would most probably
have been increased. The batting averages show a
slight falling off. Jackson, who last year had an
average of 22, takes second place with 15, but
Glanville and Steptoe show marked improvement.
Heath carries off the honours, but he has only played
in six innings. There are several young players who
claim attention, and it would do well for older mem-
bers next season to look to these rising batsmen if
they wish the club to prosper. Matcham, who only
played three innings, was not out on each occasion,
and winds up with an average of 58. The bowling
department a word of commendation is due to Glan-
ville, who has bowled admirably. Heath and Pryce
have both bowled well. If a great deal of the net
practice was abolished and scratch teams were got
together to practice, the fielding would be better. An
improvement in that respect is much needed, for if
the fielding had been smarter several matches could
have been pulled out of the fire this season. Matches
played, 12; won, 4; lost, 3; drawn, 5.

NEWBURY WEEKLY NEWS: THURSDAY 12 SEPTEMBER 1895-1.

NEWBURY CRICKET CLUB, 1895.
Thirty matches was arranged, of which 22 only were played; eight were scratched (six by opponents two by Newbury). The General Election caused Newbury to scratch their two. Of the matches played 15 were won, 4 were lost, and 3 drawn. A record was established by Newbury winning their last six matches consecutively, which included every match (five in number) in the cricket week. Mr. C. E. Sloock's 56 wickets for 523 runs per wicket was a very fine performance. In the six last matches (including the cricket week ones) the players were all bonafide members of the Newbury Cricket Club, and with very few exceptions were local men. The captain (Mr. J. L. Flint) is entitled to a word of praise. It is no doubt greatly due to his tact and knowledge of the members and of their capabilities, that the club did so well. The teams have, so far as one can judge, never done otherwise than played together in a thoroughly good and sportsmanlike spirit, the result showing that “unity is strength.”

NEWBURY WEEKLY NEWS. THURSDAY 12 SEPTEMBER 1895-2

CRICKET.

Mr. Shepherd's XII. beat Woolley Park.
This match was played at Woolley Park on Wednesday. Woolley going in first put together the useful 67, of which Rupert and Smith did best with 17 and 14 respectively. Mr. Shepherd's team, then went in the course of lunch time, making 84 in far quicker time and were they on top and looked far their game. The innings closed for 52, woolley again in again got on 18. Mr. Shepherd's men now requiring 32 runs to win, collided them with just over 3 wickets. Hutchings made a top well. Both teams were kindly entertained to tea after the match by Mr. Wroughton. Score:

Inkpen beat Falkland C.C.
The visitors in view to the Inkpen C.C. on their own ground were rather late in coming, the time fixed for the match being two o'clock, while the game did not commence till about four. The home team won the toss and play quickly began. The changes in innings looked rather dull at one time, four wickets were down for 20 runs. F. Ranger soon turned the tide, and together with T. H. D. Butler carried the ball a long way. T. H. D. Butler was taken and bowled by one, and when the innings was closed the Inkpen C.C. Butler and J. Hopkins did not bat. The visitors were dismissed for 27 runs, mainly owing to the fine fast bowling of T. May, who took 7 wickets. High score being 19. Score:

Stockcross beat Cheveley.
In lovely weather this return match, we played at Stockcross on Saturday last, and after 6 very pleasant game was won by the home team by 35 runs, Cheveley, going in the wickets first and disposed of for 34 runs, Messrs. J. Lech, E. Lech, and T. Wright being top scorers, while the bowling honours were shared by Messrs. Winterton, D. West and F. Smith, the last named taking three wickets for one run. Lambourn beat Chilton.
The return match was played on Saturday last, on the Lambourn ground, and, as the score will show, resulted in a win for Lambourn, they however this time avenging their defeat in the previous match. The game did not commence till rather late, and consequently had to be decided on the first innings. The weather was delightful and the wicket really good. Chilton won the toss, but elected to lead the home team in. A very poor start was made, as two Lambourn wickets went down for 0, but a wonderful different complexion was put on the game, when, after H. Penfold had scored 7 in good style, F. Harris and J. Bryant got well set. F. Harris made some splendid hits, and the spectators loudly cheered his lovely play, his score of 35 being made in a very short time. J. Bryant played capital cricket for his 32, and was greatly applauded upon his retirement. V. Hobbs and C. J. Murtly restored what resistance to the home team the latter was declared closed at 128. The Chilton team did but little, only one player (S. Pynter) obtaining double figures. The bowling of V. Harris, Hobbs and Bryant was very effective, but F. Harris made two capital catches in the long field. Chilton followed on, and at the call of time no wicket had fallen, the score being 61, H. New and Rumball having scored well during the innings. Brimpton beat Bradenham.
This match was played at the Bradenham ground on the Friday before last, and the weather was all that could be desired. Brimpton won the toss and decided to go in first. Their innings closed for 48, Lang and Ashby being chiefly instrumental in obtaining this total. The home team then went in and quickly succumbed, the total only reaching 46. Brimpton then added 17, made by Weaver and E. Rose, but were again all out; and Bradenham, requiring 19 to win, were 17 when time was called. Score:

Newtown beat Park Church Institute.
This return match was played in the beautiful grounds of Sandham Park, on Saturday. About 150 there being a goodly number of spectators present, including Lady Bailer and family and company. Newtown won first to the wicket, and got poor play and hard hitting on the part of E. Hicks 27, and Gardiner 24, made a total of 82 runs against bowling being too good for them, he being all bowled up by Matthew and Kevin. On the Institute sending out with wickets however, they were never dangerous either for 30 runs, Victor being top scorer with 16. Gibbs, Hicks, Ashley and Bayington, being the bowlers. They had some practice of one or two over, and were no wickets, but the Institute not being able to go in again, the home team won a pleasant game on the first innings by eight runs.

Andover House beat Newtown House.
On Thursday afternoon a match was played between elevens of the Addbury House and Newtown House, the home being won by the Addbury House eleven, a result being—lady due to the good bowling of F. Harper. James and J. Gassis; G. Cooper through six a beautiful catch at cover point, and a score of five runs. At the losers M. Stratford, White, Street and Weeks occupied the crease very well. A capital tea was hospitably provided in the house over the ground to which the players and visitors sat. A together a most enjoyable afternoon was spent, and a hearty vote of thanks was carried with acclamation to Mr. Walter Arney at his kindness. Score:

CRICKET.
HECKFIELD v. MAJOR MILDMAY’S XI.—Played at High-
field Park. Heckfield, on September 10, and resulted in
an easy victory for the home team, a fact mainly due
to an excellent innings by Bye, marred only by a single
mistake. For the visitors, Major Mildmay played sound
cricket for twenty-seven. A large and fashionable gather-
ing watched the game with much interest. Score:—

FARINGDON ADVERTISER: SATURDAY 2 NOVEMBER 1895.

CRICKET CLUB—The annual dinner of the Lech-
lade Cricket Club, was held at the New Inn Hotel,
on Thursday evening last, about 24 members and
friends sat down to the very excellent repast pro-
vided by Mrs Richens, to which ample justice was
done. The proceedings were presided over by Mr
H. W. Prior-Wandesford, who was supported by
Captain Toeswill, Dr. J. O. March, Mr W.
Crosland, the vice-chair being occupied by Mr E.
Milward. It being the first time the president
had been present at the dinner, he most generously
provided after dinner a very old-fashioned but
acceptable drink viz., “rum punch,” with which
that toast were drunk. The following was the
toast list: “The Queen,” by the chairman, “The
President,” by Mr H. Milward, responded to by
the chairman, “Lechlade Cricket Club,” by the
chairman, responded to by Mr S. Campbell and Mr
G. A. Davis, who, as is usual, read the averages
for batting and bowling during the season, “Donor
of Prize,” by Mr Davis, responded to by Mr H.
Milward and Mr S. Campbell, “Tradesmen of
Lechlade,” by Captain Toeswill, responded to by
Mr F. Stroud, “The Visitors,” by Mr Crosland,
responded to by Dr. J. O. March, “The Ladies,”
by Mr T. Slatter, responded to by Mr E. Bowley,
“Mrs Richens,” by Mr B. F. Innocent, responded
to by Mr Richens, “Vice-President” (Mr H. Mil-
ward), by the chairman, “Captain,” by Mr Davis,
responded to by Mr B. F. Innocent. During the
evening, Mr Campbell and Mr Milward presented
the bat and ball, which was won by Mr W. Johns,
to his father, Mr J. Johns, to be forwarded. Some
capital songs were sung by the following—Captain
Toeswill, Mr W. Crosland, Messrs. B. F. Innocent,
Gibbs, Andon, and Davis.

MAIDENHEAD ADVERTISER: WEDNESDAY 13 NOVEMBER 1895.

MAIDENHEAD CRICKET CLUB.

The Batting and Bowling Averages.
We have received the batting and bowling averages of the above club. The first eleven have played 20 matches, of which ten were won, four drawn and six lost. The club scored 2,725 runs for 202 wickets, an average of 13.87 per wicket, whilst their opponents scored 2,024 runs for 221 wickets, an average of 11.17 per wicket. BRECON AND RADNOR COUNTY TIMES: FRIDAY 30 AUGUST 1895.-2

LOCAL SPORT.
CRICKET.-BRECON v. LLANDOVERY.
This match was played at Llandovery on Wednesday the 21st inst. Brecon batted first and made a poor show, being all dismissed for 40. D. T. Jones took 6 wickets for 20. Llandovery were dismissed for the comparative-ly small total of 55, W. Ll. Thomas taking most of the wickets. Brecon fared little better in their second innings, being only able to compile 52. This left Llandovery 7 to win, and they lost 3 wickets before they got that number. The wicket was in a very bad condition and played badly. Score:-

The Wycombe J.X.C.C. v. O.C. play Wycombe Blue Club on the Rye to-morrow (Saturday). Wickets pitched at 2.30.
Wycombe First XI. have no fixture, nor pleasure, but in future we go to Marlow to play Bourne School (return). On Thursday—not Wednesday as at first arranged—the Grimshaw school first and second play the Wycombe Club, as there seemed no fear that Mr. and Mrs. Peachell have kindly agreed to provide luncheon and tea for the teams. This match ought to prove a good one as the first eleven of the Club-First XI. are old boys and will play for the School. We also hear that on Saturday week, when the final in the Bartick Cup competition takes place, the Vose and Mrs. Shaw intend inviting all the members of the Club to partake of tea. Mrs. Shaw has consented to present the Cup and medals. The conclusion of the game, but we shall be able next to give fuller details of the arrangements for the day.

Old John’s C.C. play the West End United on the home ground to-morrow at 2.30.—St. John’s C.C. meet matches for the Saturday in August.—R. Ford, West End road, gives no.

Church Runs O.O. play Wheeler End Blue Star, at Wheeler End, to-morrow, at 3.30.

SOUTH BUCKS FREE PRESS: FRIDAY 9 AUGUST 1895-3.

HIGH WYCOMBE v. MR. E. STEVENS' XI.
On Saturday Mr. Edmund Stevens, of The Vache, Chalfont
St. Giles, brought over a strong team to oppose the local club,
but rain prevented the game from being played out. It was,
however, drawn in favour of Wycombe, who had made 43 for
the loss of two wickets, when stumps were drawn. To play
the possible before luncheon, and a start was not made till
past 2 o'clock, when the visitors won the toss and began
their innings and concluded, a smart shower compelled them
to make a precipitate rush to the friendly shelter of the
pavilion. The rain holding off for three hours the innings
of the finished, 87 runs being the result. On Wycombe going
in the light was very bad, and the rain came down at intervals
in torrents, and the local captain was obliged to play out the
was thought best to leave the game drawn. At that point the
match was left in the position shown by the following score
and analysis. Jewer and not Mace played fresh and very
some good strokes, his 29 including a 5, two 4's three 3's, and
two 2's:-

RAYNERS v. PERMANENT STAFF OF THE 2nd
BATT. OXFORD LIGHT INFANTRY.
On Monday last, August 5th, a match was played on
Rayners private ground between the local team and the
body stationed a little by the mounted recruits, under the
victory for the former by an innings and 11 runs.
A. V. W. Hodd appeared the best batter, and, showed well
throughout, while C. D. Powell was very slow at the
commencement, and a good wicket was lost for 34, but when
we Captain and Mr. Powell became associated, the best stand
of the day was made, and some good cricket was seen, both
playing with confidence. They put on 62 runs between them,
when Mr. Rose was caught at the wicket for an invaluable 37.
Powell left soon after with a well-played 39 to his credit;
Wheeler made 14 and the remaining bats disposed of quickly
disposed of, the innings closed for 114. An adjournment was
now made for lunch, which had been served (in a spacious
marquee erected for the occasion), though the committee of
the Philip and Lady Rose after ample justice had been done
to the good things provided, the visitors commenced their
innings. Captain Rose and Dash were the only pair to
pose to show any resistance to the attack of O. M. Rose and
Powell, who were bowling in their best form, and the innings
closed for 51. Captain Rose's 16 was the best way the little
batting display, while backed well, a game drive out of the
ground. Powell had the best analysis, taking 6 wickets for
22, while for Rose 3 cost 28 runs. Rayners to follow on
they failed to reach the number required to save an innings'
defeat. Dean taking 4 wickets for 13 runs, and the game
realised a more varied. Full score and analysis:-

Cricket.

WYCOMBE v. ORIEL.
A team from what had hango[d], Bad, Balnes, Mumford,
Radley, and De Zyl, R. D. Shaw were absentees did not look
on paper strong enough in do battle successfully for Wycombe
when they met the Oriel club on Tuesday. However,
with the assistance of C. Langley and G. Langley—the latter
playing for his brother—and W. Stone, a Wycombe man,
who, since his residence in the Midlands, has been tried in
the Warwickshire Colts team, they managed to win on the
first innings by 47 runs, to which Keen contributed 33 and
Stone 22, and for other batsmen bagged the double figures,
as that when the last wicket fell the total had reached 131.
Unfortunately, Parr was unable to bowl, having twisted his
knee in turning to make his late run, and Keen and G.
Langley bowled with such effect that Fold and W. H. Percival
were the only two among the visitors who made anything
approaching a stand against their deliveries, and the whole
side were disposed of for 84. The bowling of the Oriel men
in Wycombe’s second innings was somewhat loose, and got
severely punished, as shown by the subjoined score and
analysis:—

Y.M.C.A. held at Ascot’s C.C. on the Wycombe Saturday,
at 7.15.
Wycombe Lawn Tennis Fete.—A general meeting of the above
was held on Tuesday, July 30, to consider the fact that after
the Junior League was started some dissension it was proposed
and carried. It was decided to adjourn the matter for
further time, at the Red Lion, at 8 o’clock. All members are
requested to attend, as the business will be chairman by Mr.
Guy (who paid all).

CHALFONT PARK v. ST. HELEN (LONDON).—The annual
match was played between the above at Chalfont Park on
the 6th, and resulted in a win for the home team by six wickets
to comparatively comprehensive the number they had to do to
lead with (71). Sidney Golding played specially crafty, and
got out in the first and at the second innings. Tom Worley
captainly, taking 15 wickets for 18 runs. The visitors certainly
were very weak. Ashton bowled fairly well for them. Chalfont
made 84 to the visitor’s 71 all for six wickets in the
second. The visitors twenty-one were all got off for 56.
Bowled: W. Portal. The CHALFONT (LONDON).—The return
match of the above on Monday last was the visitors’
won. Earle Shiloh (?) caught for the visitors, was very clever.
W. Summers looked lively, but was all out for 42. Tommy
Worley got 6 for 35, and F. Ainslie 6 for 25. Both
sides were taking 6 for 30 runs. Kemball 3 for 14 and Miller
4 for 10. The Portal team fared better than their opponents,
scoring 47 to 48. W. H. G. (A?) and Bousden (3) did
best. Balding took 6 for 14 and Jenner 4 for 14. October
Park, Barnham scored 61 for the loss of 4 wickets, and J.
Wheeler, Baker (5) not out, Woodley (14), Baldwin (14) and
Hall (3) not out) united in line form. Hall, however, dropped
rather pl. and the Telegraph Staff then won by 8 runs on
the first innings. Mack’s captured 3 wickets for 36 runs.

TAPLOW BISTERS v. BATTERSEA SOCIAL.—Played on the
Briers’ Ground on Saturday, the home team winning easily.
After disposing of the visitors for 29 (T. Smith 12), Taplow
scored 94 for 6 wickets when the game was stopped by rain.
H. Pilcher made 16, G. Jones 10 not out, and Goodman 9. The
two Bowers, Fisher obtained 7 wickets for 30 runs, from 8 1/2
overs, and J. Wright 1 for 14. For Battersea Rooke (5) and
A. Garrett (4) did best, and hadbeenallround.

CULTAS GLEE v. GERRARDS CROSS.—This popular match
was played on the charming ground at Eversley. Scores
showed somewhat one-sided, with the Greens easily on
the winning each was played. The visitors scored 69. Gerrards
Cross put together 117 and won by 48 runs. G. Piggott
made 21 and G. Lamb 36 for the home team. The Wooburn
hospitality to the players was much appreciated.

FLACKWELL HEATH 2nd XI. v. LITTLE MARLOW.
LOW SCORING.
A match between the above clubs was played on the ground of the latter on Saturday last and resulted in a victory for Flackwell Heath by 25 runs on the first innings. The batting of the latter, and Smith, was very good. Almond occupied the wickets, taking 3 wickets in a very creditable manner. No doubt the result would have been different had time permitted a second innings for the victors. Bowlers and fielders did good form. In the second innings of Flackwell Heath Almond again occupied the bat first and took 6 wickets for 12. Many obtained 1 to 8 runs. Scores:-

MARLOW v. HIGH WYCOMBE.
BIG HITTING BY E. B. MARSL.
The return match between the old rivals was played at Marlow on Saturday. In the weather, or wickets that favoured the bowler, it will be remembered that in the first match at Wycombe which drawn much in favour of Marlow. On this occasion the riverside team fielded an easy victory, thanks to a fine innings by E. B. Marsden, by Langley’s brilliant catch to dismiss V. Waller with one hand, and some excellent bowling by W. H. Lamoon and Barber. Marlow won the toss, Langley and Barber facing the deliveries of Payne and B. B. Parker. These quickly sent the total registered 24, when both batsmen were out with a dozen to their credit. Marsden and Lamoon followed the total to 56, when the latter was caught by Waller, and a Barber failed to score and Want only hit a 4. Five wickets were down for 62. Bowes then came to the aid of Marsden, and after a useful venture of 15 to Want’s 9 added cheers, but with four needed. A great chance came over the team. E. B. Parker sending back Bowes, Brown, and Mackenzie in one over. On this over Parker had a marvellous with a tremendous force, and was specially severe on Payne, driving his to six into Court’s adjoining close. The score was 144. Bowes field, it was doubtful but until the total was 149, when he was yorked by Parker. Just when it appeared certain that Marlow would take out the lead, he was captured in the slips, and the innings closed for 146. Marsden’s closing score of 86 included two 6’s, eight 4’s, two 3’s, and eight 2’s. He was carefully applauded on retiring to the pavilion. Both Parker and Kean bowled well. Wycombe commenced their innings with T. M. Parker and Langley. The bowlers were W. H. Lamoon and Barber. At more disastrous start could not well be imagined, Langley caught and bowled Parker and clean bowled Barker in his first over. The first 4 (through Want) couple of singles, and Langley was too caught by Mackenzie at Barber. Three for 2. E. B. Parker helped George to put a better aspect upon affairs, but the former was at 16 at first single of 16. Jada followed in and was bowled by Lamoon at 28. T. Brothers George then got together and carried the score to 44 when Want made full-length draw catches and Waller, at close but well. Page hit up 14 by means of a 6, 4, and two 2’s, and the innings closed for 60. Lamoon bowled tremendously well, his overs wickets costing 61 runs each. Wycombe followed on, and made 50 for one wicket. Langley batted well for 35 not out. Marlow therefore won by 95 runs on the first innings - a rather one-sided result, seeing that the teams which was in the field was by no means a strong one. Scores and analyses:-

HIGH WYCOMBE v. WOOBURN INSTITUTE.
This match, which was played on the Wooburn ground last Saturday, at one time looked as if one side or the other would have ended in favour of the home team. The visitors were wickets before the London and other trap. of J. Bacon, who proved a tower of strength to them in both departments of the game. Wycombe did no play their full strength, some of their best men being reserves. The home side went in first, and a total of 154 was made before they were all disposed of. The chief scorers were G. A. George 37; J. Humphrey 28; and Blood 16. C. A. Greenham and G. V. Goodwin also played by Bird, C. Ford, and Pryor had cover. Bacon delivered. one the chief of the game of the day in taking 7 wickets for 31. his principal supporters in the Wooburn, and they added 33 before the first wicket. G. A. George soon got rid of Greenham. Bacon’s bowling compelled several stops. Burying the opening speed he got the last three wickets obtained without a run being scored off him. For Wooburn Institute, Percy Bowler and Plummer played well, the second named hitting G. George for six when the game was in the balance. The side looked more dangerous, as the two at wickets had put on not out eight runs between them. Percy was the most successful with the ball but his four wickets were nearly all clean bowled. MARLOW v. MR. J. MONRO WALKER'S XI.
On Saturday Marlow met an eleven of together by Mr. J. Monro Walker, of Bisham Abbey, on the Marlow ground. The weather was delightfully fine, and a enjoyable game ensued. The visitors won by 125, and took 171 in their first innings. Bartlett hit hard for 50, and the major contributions from all the side except Lane. Browne put out before he had scored, the total reached 335, Marlow with 2 (four for all) overthrow and four byes. Monro Walker was credited with an 8 (four for all) overthrows. Marlow lost Pains and Vallance cheaply, but who struck out Lane, G. Owen, Ballie, and Watts, the visitors’ total was passed with six wickets down. Eventually the innings closed for 183. Lane one of the Australian visitors played at Marlow at 4.15 o’clock and threw in his dashing score of 48. Largely his drive in his 50. Mr. Walker took 2 wickets by 50 runs on the first innings. WYCOMBE HILLS v. WANDERERS v. HOLLOWAY'S BOOT OPERATIVE CO.
The return match between the above-named clubs which took place at Holmer Green on Saturday last was won by the Hills on the first innings by 65 runs. The Wanderers had a strong team, and although, thanks to the excellent play of W. Waller and P. Bell and H. Puddy, they made a good stand, their total of 66 was well below that of the hills. Shortly after, Lyne, Croxford, Fenn, Berry, J. Young and Bright, who all played in brilliant form, helped the Hills to put together 132, the highest score made by any side this season. F. L. Berry, A. Bright, Bell, and Lynch were the principal scorers. Holloway’s closed for 31. The attack for these was weak and the Hills made 50 in the first innings, and when Thomas joined in the slaughter he had all previous batters. H. Moore made 16, but no more. The visitors made 132 in the first innings. The company’s men at the second innings only totalled 26. Both Lyne and Hensbury, who bowled through the innings, captured 6 wickets each for 20 and 7. GERRARDS CROSS v. AMERSHAM.
The return match was played at Gerrards Cross on August 2nd, and resulted in a victory for the home team by 67 runs. Bagley played excellent cricket for his 62, and it was noticed up by Lowe, who batted well. After the match Bagley was presented with a sum of money collected from the spectators in appreciation of his valuable innings. Golding handled the ball well, his analysis reading 11.3 overs, 2 maidens, 21 runs, 5 wickets. For the visitors, Willoughby and Wingfield did well. Scores—

MR. W. PEARCE’S (WYCOMBE) XI. v. SOUTHALL.
On Saturday last Mr. W. Pearce, of the “Nag’s Head,” London-road, captained an eleven to visit Southall to try conclusions with an eleven representing the Southall Club (York. Although the Beckham side did innings have 118 runs to their credit, Southall were far and away the best team, and for the loss of only 3 wickets they had contributed 157. Dixon and Hudson were said to be classed as belonging to the Middlesex team of Colt, and the way in which Dixon contributed his 76 showed that he was a batsman of no mean order. His total included one 6, three 4’s, fifteen 3’s, and five 2’s. William Cooper, too, looked up quite boundary in succession. In fact, against such formidable opponents the home team were Wycombe representatives were little to amount for, nevertheless one pitched game was the result. Both W. Pearce and G. W. Harper showed good form for the losers. Score and analysis:-

GREAT MISSENDEN v. LEE COMMON.
The return match was played at Great Missenden on Thursday August 22. The visitors won the toss, starting with F. Lewis and S. Ayres. Both played well, the former occupying defending the wicket for the whole of the innings and carrying his bat out, his highest score and four 4’s. J. was put, and singles. S. Ayres made a useful 16. For the home eleven W. Webb played well, and was smartly caught after making 14. Dr. Turnor played a nice cricket to 8 and David was the best bowler. Scores:-

MR. COLLINS CLASS v. BOOKER TEMPERANCE.
The return match between these clubs took place at Booker on Saturday last, and pleasant game resulted in a win for the Class by eight runs on the first innings. The match at these teams has usually been a close game; last year it was a win for the Class and a drawn match, and this year the result of the fixture has been the same. Batting first, the Class made 50, J. Keen (32) and Collins (10) being chief contributors. Booker then went in, and the total had reached 27 when the last wicket fell, out of which number Burnham had made 14. In their second venture the Class could only compile 27, neither batsman being able to make a “card” against the under-arm bowling of J. Pearce; Bather (15) was the only one to get into double figures. Score:-

MARRIED v. SINGLE.
On Tuesday the second match was played upon the same ground between Eleven Married and Eleven Single. Mr Hore himself taking the bat with the Married Eleven. It was a well contested game, the Single team being the victors by 3 runs only. F. Baker was successful with both ball and bat. Refreshments were dispensed to players and spectators, and in the evening a substantial supper was provided for all that had taken part in the game. About 50 sat down, and Mr Hore joined the company. The tables being cleared, Mr Blake, in appropriate words, proposed the health of the host, which was drunk with musical honours. A social and harmonious evening was spent, such as Sutton cricketers have not often the opportunity of spending. Score :-

Cambridge Express: Saturday 3 August 1895 - 3

SPORT AND PLAY.

GOSSIP UPON CURRENT SPORTS
AND PASTIMES.

I am vain enough to think that some of my readers have missed "Vim's" notes from the columns of the Express during the last fortnight. To them I offer an apology for my non-appearance in print. Like the majority of people, I caught the election fever, and, becoming absorbed in the progress of the fight, had no time to expend upon such mundane things as athletic notes. I am afraid I have rather got out of touch with the progress of events in the athletic world during the last fortnight, but will do my best to make up lost ground.

* *

My first duty is to express both pleasure and regret at the doings of the County Cricket Club. The drubbing the County team received from the M.C.C. and Ground was a severe one, although the Club team was not a particularly strong one. These onerous collapses of our County teams are unexplainable by me, although those who are behind the scenes may be able to give a reason. With a somewhat stronger eleven, the County fave Hunts. on Wednesday a ditto to the treatment they had received from the M.C.C., viz., a single innings defeat. The record for the season thus far is one win and one loss. On Monday and Tuesday next, the County will entertain the M.C.C. and Ground at Cambridge, and it is to be hoped that they may be able to give a better account of themselves then.

The old suggestion has been revived in the select circle of enthusiasts of the game of the desirability of playing at least one County match each season upon Parker's Piece. The Herts. match was peculiarly suited to such treatment, and it is a pity that it was not played on the public ground, and used to excite a greater interest amongst Cambridge people in the doings of the Club, the future of which looks none too rosy at present.

* *

The final of the Cambridgeshire Cricket Cup Competition will again be fought out by the Old Higher Grade, last year's winners, and the Camden. The old boys are such good sportsmen that one would like to see them win again, but, on the other hand, the Camden have been in the competition since the very commencement, and have had a great run of ill-luck, and their win would be a popular one. The final promises once more to be an extremely interesting one.

The scratching of the Cassandra Club in this Competition has caused a good deal of public comment. I have had a conversation with the secretary, who declines to state why the Club scratched, although he affirms that they had good and sufficient reason for so doing, which I do not doubt. After all, action of this kind is the Club's private business, but it seems a pity the Cassandra should have knocked out the old Persians, who would have gone through, and then have retired without vouchsafing any reason for so doing.

I am really sorry for Sawston, who were so crushingly defeated by the Old Higher Grade last Saturday. What could have come over the Institute team? The whole side was disposed of for 11 runs, six of these being extras, and the only man who scored off the bat was Bailey.

I am informed that the suggested dates for the final are August 22nd and 23rd, but it has not yet been decided whether the match shall be played on Parker's Piece or the University Ground.

Histon and Impington v. J. Teas of the Old Higher Grade C.C.-This match was played at Histon, when the home team added one more victory to their list of matches played this season. Up to the present they have only lost one match. For the winners Mr. Walter Crane performed the "hat trick." Scores:-

CAMBRIDGE EXPRESS: SATURDAY 10 AUGUST 1895-2.

COUNTY v. BOROUGH POLICE.
The annual match between cricketing teams representing the Borough and County of Cambridge Police Forces took place on Wednesday, when the policemen journeyed to Royston and spent a pleasant time on the Heath. The County went first to the wicket, and made 50, to which P.-c. F. Brooks largely contributed. The Borough then scored 68. Then followed a piece of good cricket, in which the brothers P.-c. F. and G. Brooks hit away in dashing style, and they were so well supported by Inspector Webb and P.-c. Carter that 69 runs for the loss of three wickets were registered quickly, after which stumps were drawn. The Borough thus obtained a victory on the first innings. The bowling was chiefly notable for p.-c. Rackham's analysis of 6 for 15 runs for the Borough, and p.-c. F. Brooks's 6 for 25 for the County. At the close of play the party sat down to lunch at the White Horse.

SPORT AND PLAY.
GOSSIP UPON CURRENT SPORTS
AND PASTIMES.

A well-known writer on sport sends me the follow-
ing particulars of Kumar Shri Ranjitsinhji:-In
a memorable cricket season the performance of
K. S. Ranjitsinhji (or the famous Indian prince
to be known, instead of by Prince) have created
almost as much attention as the doings of
the great "W. G.". Hailing, as he is familiarly
called in University cricket, came over from
India some few seasons ago, and lived for a year
or so with the Rev. Louis Robinson, "precentor of
Trinity College. In October, 1889, he matriculated
as a Non-Col. in the University of Cambridge,
but, though taking to cricket, few opportunities
presented themselves for displaying his abilities.
In due course he entered the foundation of
Trinity (????), but exceptions and occasional
match for the 2nd Eleven he was little known in
the cricket world until he became associated with
Cundall and other Town Clubs, when he imme-
diately shot into prominence, and a great future
was predicted for him. In the year 1892, neither
"Varsity nor College could be induced to recognise
his sterling qualities. However, during that year
he had a magnificent average, and totalled over
2,000 runs, topping the century on 10 or 11
different occasions.

From the commencement of 1893 season his
exceptional prowess demanded the attention of the
Varsity authorities, and Mr. Jackson awarded
him his blue, but although he averaged 27 79 in
Varsity matches, in the Oxford and Cambridge
match he failed, as so many other great cricketers
have done. That year he was a regular member
of the Trinity 1st Eleven, and came out with the
fine figures of 71 8, eclipsing the batting achieve-
ments of Messrs Jackson, W. G. Lurie, Wells,
&c. and other scores with scores 116,
111, 104, and 02 not out. He was preparing for
the County of Cambs. in the '93 and '94 season,
but froth want of an extensive programme and
other causes did not shine very conspicuously.
He played in several first-class matches last
season and came out eighth, with an average of
32 63 for 15 innings, and altogether secured in cen-
turies, viz., 182, 146 not out, 137 not out, 123 not out,
115 not out, and 103 not out. While known but
little in first-class matches, his services during
last winter were sought by several counties, but
having residential qualification for Sussex he
decided to throw in his lot with that county.
It will suffice to record the fact that this season,
up to August 3rd, he had totalled in all matches
2,117 runs, with an average of over 70, and in
first-class matches up to the date mentioned he
averaged 53.22, with an aggregate of 1,497, and
the following innings figure in his large total of
206 not out, 174 not out, 150, 137 not out, 110, and
100. The last four centuries are first-class. Space
will not permit of further reference to his efforts
with various other Clubs to which he belongs. On
his day he is able to send down a good ball, and
his early fame was established through his
brilliant fielding at short-slip.

K. S. Ranjitsinhji, born in September, 1872, is,
the record is, of the Jala of Nawanagar, and in,
the interior, in his 23rd year. His principal home
in this country is Cambridge, where, during the
winter months, he diligently participates in shoot-
ing and fishing. He is also a very good billiard
player, and good judges have asserted that had he
have taken more keenly to tennis and racquets he
would have represented his 'Varsity against
Oxford in either pastime.

Ranjitsinhji, whose mode of living is an ex-
ample which might well be followed by a num-
ber of cricketers, being a non-smoker and almost
total abstainer at the same time in one of the
most jovial and unassuming fellows to meet; he
been supporter of all legitimate recreation; a
severe critic on cricket, and very enthusiastic
in all sports he indulges in.

Whether K. S. Ranjitsinhji retires to his
native province at the end of this season re-
mains to be seen. However, it is contended that
he is too far infatuated and too great an exponent
of cricket to be able to tear himself from a
game in which he is so conspicuous at the present
moment, and the wish of all sportsman is at least
England will witness his prowess for many years
to come.

* * *
The County of Cambs. Cricket Eleven cannot
yet steer clear of rough luck, and had it been
possible to complete the return match with
M.C.C. and Ground, possibly they would have
experienced considerable trouble in staying the
game. Had the Marylebone Club taken under
the same conditions as Cambs. they would not
have made 243. The two Butlers (who are likely
to be most useful for the County), Barnes' 118, and
Davey backed well, especially the Notts. veteran
W. G. Grace, jun., who captured the M.C.C.
eleven, bowled with success.

Shortly the third tie for the Cambs. Cricket
Association Cup will be played, the contesting
clubs being the holders-the Old Higher Grade-
and the Camden. Both clubs command the
respect of all votaries of the game, and the latter
of either will be popular. The Camden, it is
stated, have never given the Association any
trouble, and have always been loyal to the
Committee. They have frequently figured in the
final stages, and are fully deserving of meeting
with success. This equally applies to the "Old
Boys," for whom P. Cornell has accomplished
some truly wonderful feats with the ball of late,
capturing six wickets for one run and seven
for ten.

For them P. Luff is also a useful performer, and
many think both he and Cornell should have
received trials for the County. For the Camden
O'Connor is the main cause for hope. Against
Hunts. the county's pro. actually captured 11
wickets for 80 runs. Should he be able to repeat
his best efforts the "Old Boys" would have any-
thing but an easy task.

Several fairly good bats appear for each eleven,
and everything points to an interesting game, and
we hope no game will permit of the best side
winning.

K. S. Ranjitsinhji informs me he he will not be
able to play any local cricket till after the Sussex
programme is completed, when he hopes to be
able to take part in afternoon matches.

The leading dozen batsmen and their averages
at the commencement of the week were :
Times. Most
Not Innings. Outs. Runs. Ins. Aver.

The changes from the previous week were that
A. E. Stoddart and G. Brann qualified for the
first d.z., in H. W. Bainbridge and H. K. Foster
making way. The old Etonian, however, is the
third Cambridge man to score 1,000 runs in first-
class matches. Such a feat may have previously
been accomplished, but I never heard of it, and
P. S. Jackson was the only Cambridge man to
reach those figures last year with 1020 for '93
innings. As N. F. Druce, Lord Hawke, Hayward,
Carpenter, and F. S. Jackson have several more
matches to play, it is quite possible they may join
Messrs. Ranjitsinhji, Woods, and Bainbridge.

There is every prospect of Tom Hayward
joining out to South Africa with George Lohmann's
team at the end of the season. I hear Tom is
anxious to bring a team down to Cambridge at
the end of the season. There was some talk of a
match last April between K. S. Ranjitsinhji's XI.
and Tom Hayward's, and such a return in September,
now, with strong sides, should prove a great
attraction.

CAMBRIDGE BOROUGH POLICE v. CAMBS.
COUNTY POLICE.
On Wednesday these Clubs met in a return match on Trinity College Ground. The County went to the wicket first, but were dismissed for 24. For the Borough Williamson secured five wickets for nine runs, and Rackham five for 10 runs. In the second innings Williamson got six wickets for 22, and Rackham three for 23. Brooks and Taylor divided the wickets for the County. An excellent lunch was provided for the players and friends. The following are the scores:

STOCKPORT V. WERNETH.
Stockport met Werneth, on the ground of the
latter, for the first time this season before a
grand gate of over two thousand spectators, and in
charming weather. Both teams were all too
prevailed. Werneth were minus the services
of Wartenby, one of their pros., but had Brooks,
of the Lancashire side and late of Stockport,
assisting them, and who did very well
too, taking five wickets for just over six runs a
piece. The Werneth captain being fortunate
in winning the toss sent in Brodie and Barrow to
face the bowling of Brown and F. Torkington.
Both men scored a boundary each off Hodgkinson,
but the more audacious Barrow was caught out
grandly caught by Herty. Rowe's square leg.
22—1. Bell, the popular Werneth pro., came
next, but after scoring a single he was magnificently
caught at slip by F. Tyler. 26—2. Leyswith
followed him and more good cricket was seen.
Both men played well, showing Brown in fine
with the trickiness and the ball. At 46 a change
of bowling was tried, F. Tyler going on for F.
Torkington. The separation, however, came from
the other end, Sam Brown bowling Heyworth with
a grand ball, after that player had scored 14 in
nineteen m's. 53—3. Wickets after this fell fast,
Sam Brown being almost unplayable, the
wits being all dismissed for the
not over grand score of 98. This was due to the
splendid bowling of Sam, whose analysis reads—21
overs for 8 maidens 25 runs and 7 wickets.
The fielding of the Stockport men was also very
good, all the catches that were taken being very
fine. Stockport opened their venture by sending
in W. Bartley and J. Bate to the bowling of Hall
and Brooks. The start was at once disastrous,
Loring Bate and Arthur Torkington being only 15
runs on the board. Brown and W. Bartley soon
after fell victims, and four wickets were down
for 27 runs, but when Harold Bartley and Diney
got together a different complexion was put on the
game, as they treated the bowling with the
utmost confidence, especially the former,
the 5th wicket falling at 55, Diney being
bowled. Fred Long next joined Hartley, who
was playing a splendid game, and he also found a
good partner in Long, who also played very well.
Hartley, after playing a splendid game, was lost
unfortunately in playing on. After making 77 he was
loudly cheered on returning, the sixth wicket has
falling at 89. Little need be farther comment
except the batting of Fred Long and Frank Tyler,
the former scoring 14 and the latter 13, not out ; the
innings closing for 110—Stockport winning by just
a dozen. It was a grand match, and was fought
out right to the end very determinedly. Great
praise is due to Harold Bartley, Fred Long, and
Frank Tyler for the splendid way they kept their
wicket up against the fine bowling of the tricky
Hall and Brooks ; and Stockport have every reason
to be proud of their handsome victory, every man
being a thorough trier. Below is appended full
score and analysis.

STOCKPORT v. WERNETH (2nd Elevens).—The
Werneth are met for the first time this season at the
Oval Grove Park, in glorious weather, and before a
fair attendance. The visitors, winning the toss,
decided to bat a little after three o'clock, to the
bowling of Jones and McLachlan. Jackson opened
splendidly with Jones, but on the whole run came
slowly, eight wickets being down for 93, when
Marshall and Watson became partners and a
splendid stand was made, the score being then to
170 before either were separated, the score being
still to have when the innings closed. After the
usual interval Stockport commenced to bat a
quarter past five, with rather formidable task before
them. Any soon set to work to attempt. The first
wicket compiled 47 towards the number, May, the
earlier batsman, accounting for 43 of them. F.
Selby, the new man in, seemed rather uncomfortable
at first, but he was getting more at home when he
lost the service of Boyle, the score reading 73—2—19.
Marshall joined Selby with almost a hundred runs
wanting, and the hand of the close partner to Mr.
They had much to do, but the batsmen soon set
to work, although hitting for 4's in one over. Ex-
citement ran high in time crept on. The spectators
became quite riveted to the game, especially the
junior portion, who were enthusiastic with delight
as each hit seemed to be sent to the boundary.
It was a treat to watch Marshall play and drive;
bowler. Nothing seemed to come amiss, but
another wicket fell before the required runs were
reached, Selby being cleaned bowled by the
captain for a very useful 46. With then voices
left to get the remaining nine runs, Jones joined
Marshall, the latter soon making the winning hit
with a boundary. It was shortly afterwards bowled
for a grand 67, comprising 13 fours and 4 twos.
Time arrived soon one little wicket left, Stockport
being victorious by 11 runs and five wickets.
Werneth are very strongly represented. This was
their first defeat of the season ; but the home men
have to concede yet. Next week Stockport is
2nd journey to Cheshire Hall, and a
dis to hoped the team will be as suc-
cessful as they were on Saturday. Scores :—
Werneth: H. Jackson b McLachlan 33, F. Dixon b

STOCKPORT V. WERNETH.
Stockport met Werneth, on the ground of the
latter, for the first time this season before a
grand gate of over two thousand spectators, and in
charming weather. Both teams were well re-
presented. Werneth were, minus the services
of Wharmby, one of their pros., but had Brookes,
of the Manchester staff, paid into Stockport;
analysing them, and then what did very well
too, taking five wickets for just over nine runs a
piece. The Werneth captain being fortunate
in winning the toss sent in Redfern and Haggas to
face the bowling of Brown and Fred Torkington.
Both men scored boundary each off Torkington,
but the score had only reached 22 when Haggas was
grandly caught by Harry Rayl by square leg,
22-1-10. Hall, the popular Werneth pro, came
next, but after scoring a single he was magnificently
caught at slips by F. Tyler, 26-2-1. Heyworth
followed in and here some good cricket was seen.
Both men played well, though Brown troubled them
with his trickness with the ball. At 46 a change
of bowling was tried, F. Tyler going on for F.
Torkington. The separation, however, came from
the other end, Sam Brown bowling Heyworth with
a grand ball, after that player had scored 14; in a
nice style, 53-3-4. Wickets after this fell fast,
Sam Brown being almost unplayable, the
whole side being dismissed for the
not over grand score of 98. The was due to the
splendid bowling of Sam who analysed 21.1
overs for 8 maidens 25 runs and 7 wickets.
The fielding of the Stockport men was also very
good, all the catches that were took being very
fine. Stockport oped their venture by sending
in W. Hartley and J. Bates to the bowling of Hall
and Brookes. The start was at once disastrous,
losing Bates and Arthur Torkington with only 15
runs on the board. Brown and W. Hartley soon
after fell victims, and four good wickets were down
for 27 runs, but when Harold Hartley and Disney
got together a different complexion was put on to
the game, and they treated the bowling with the
utmost confidence, especially the former,
the fifteens falling at 55. Disney being
bowled. Fred Long next joined Hartley, who
was playing a splendid game, and he also found a
good partner in Long, who also played very well.
Hartley, after playing a splendid game, was most
unfortunate in playing on. After making 27 he was
loudly cheered on returning, the sixth wicket thus
falling at 89. Little needs for further comment,
except the batting of Fred Long and Frank Tyler,
the former scoring 14 and the latter 12, not out; the
innings closing for 110-Stockport winning by just
a dozen. It was a grand match, and was fought
out right to the end very nearly. Great
praise is due to Harold Hartley, Fred Long, and
Frank Tyler for the splendid way they kept their
wickets up against the fine bowling of the crack
Hall and Brookes; and Stockport have every reason
to be proud of their handsome victory, every man
being a thorough trier. Below is appended full
score and analysis.

STOCKPORT v. WERNETH (2nd Elevens).-These
two old rivals met for the first time this season at
Cale Green Park, in glorious weather, and before a
fair attendance. The visitors, winning the toss,
decided to bat a little after three o'clock, to the
bowling of Jones and M'Clanahan. Watson opened
splendidly with a four, but on the whole runs came
slowly, eight wickets being down for 93, when
Maresald and Watson became partners and
provided stand and made, the score being taken to
170 before either were separated; the score being
still the same when the innings closed. After the
usual interval Stockport commenced to bat at a
quarter past five, with a rather formidable task before
them. May soon set to work in earnest. The first
wicket occupied 47 towards the number. May, the
veteran batsman, accounting for 43 of these. F.
Selby, the new man in, seemed rather uncomfortable
at first, but he was getting more at home when he
lost the service of Royle, the score reading 73-2-19.
Marshail joined Selby with almost subdued runs.
Watney, and the hand of the clock pointing to six.
They had much to do, but the batsmen stood set
to work, Marshall hitting for 4's in one over. Ex-
citement ran high as time crept on. The spectators
became quite riveted to the game, especially the
junior portion, who were enthusiastic with delight
as each batsman sent the leather to the boundary.
It was a treat to watch Marshall play each from
bowler. Nothing seemed to cause him, but
N. the wicket fell before the required runs were
reached, Selby being cleaned bowled by the
captain for a very useful 46. With ten minutes
to get the remaining nine runs, Jones joined
Marshall, the latter soon making the winning hit
with a boundary. He was shortly afterwards caugh
for a grand 57, compiling 13 fours and 4 twos.
Time arrived when the fifth wicket fell, Stockport
being victorious by 11 runs and five wickets.
Werneth was very strongly represented. This was
their first defeat of the season; but the home sorters
have to come yet. Next week Stockport
2nd journey to Cheadham Hill, and it
is to be hoped the team will be as successful as they were on Saturday. Score:-

CHESHIRE COUNTY NEWS: FRIDAY 2 AUGUST 1895-2

SATURDAY'S MATCHES.
Castleton v. Stockport.
This match should have been played at Castleton,
but owing to the ground being unfit and although
the heavy rain if was cancelled. Next week the
Stockport team journey to Buxton, to try con-
clusions with the two clubs.

St. Thomas' Athletic v. Norbury 2nd.-At
Norbury. Thomas won batting first, scoring 14
all out. J. Bowden took seven wickets for five
runs. and W. Bart three for eight. J. Garner and
J. Bowden went in to bat for St. Thomas'. They
had scored 28 when rain stopped the match, leaving
St. Thomas' winners by 10 wickets and 14 runs

Castleton v. Stockport.
This match should have been played at Castleton,
but owing to the ground being unfit caused through
the heavy rains it was cancelled. Next week the
Stockport team journey to Bolton, to try conclu-
